Bullethead - Spit and vinegar badness from the whole band. Love Eddie's fills on this one. Not particularly as catchy as the rest, but only because everything else is so strong. 3/5  7. As Is - Wow, this is different, Alex drums sounds huge and Eddie's playing opens in a dropped tuning that sounds even lower than drop D! Then the band kicks in at a furious pace with a killer Ed riff. Props to David Lee Roth for coming up with lyrics that keep up with the pace of the song. Love the breakdown at 2:40 and DLR 'Love 'em all I say, let Cupid sort 'em out'. 4/5  8. Honeybabysweetiedoll - Wild noise intro leads to a very heavy sounding riff and Eddie screaming some harmonics. May be the darkest and heaviest thing I've ever heard from the band. 3.5/5  9. The Trouble With Never - A classic sounding chorus on this one, with a 2012 version of Jimi Hendrix for the wah tinged verse riff. DLR sounds like he had to squeeze in some of the lyrics to fit the timing. Another cool breakdown (this album is FULL of these!) at 2:17 and DLR speaking the lyrics low and cool. Good stuff. 4/5  10. Outta Space - The verse sections are classic sounding VH1 or 2, but the chorus is new sounding. Another vintage killer solo from Eddie. And did you EVER imagine you'd hear DLR throwing out a reference to his facebook page! Not particularly hooky but still cool. 3/5  11. Stay Frosty - If I had to pick a single #1 favorite, this is it. Wow. Just killer from beginning to end. Starts out with an Ice Cream Man bluesy acoustic guitar and DLR with some BRILLIANT vocal phrasing, total vintage VH. Then at 1:12 the back kicks in with a HUGE, in your face sound , Eddie's guitar just killer sounding and the rhythym section of Alex and Wolfgang locked in perfectly. All the swagger and awesomeness of the old days. 5/5  12. Big River - And from the previous tunes badness, it doesn't stop, Big River stomps in with more classic Van Halenisms. Not my favorite breakdown in this one, but another scorcher solo from Ed. 4/5  13. Beats Workin' - And to cap it , Beats Workin' big bad riffing from Eddie and a catchy chorus. Slightly anti-climatic after Stay Frosty and Big River but the hanging ending note from Eddie caps it all. 3.5.5  So there you have it, a return to glory if ever there was one and as much as I like Chickenfoot too, this album just 1 ups their two records in every possible way.

Treat anything you read in this guide with extreme skepticism.<br /><br />\\"Get the Rough Guide, not the Lonely Planet.\\"  This is the advice I read most often nowadays. B006ZDU7QI|5.0|I bought this for the singles Somebody I Used to Know and Easy Way Out. Those songs are great, but I was pleased when I found that the rest of the disc is an absolute treasure. In fact, I think every track is fantastic, save for perhaps the brief opener. I'm shocked at how good each song is, and equally shocked to read a review on here that says something along the lines of each song sounding the same. I don't think that could be further from the truth! Gotye skips genres or at least influences from one song to the next. Easy Way Out reminds me of a Beck jam, Somebody that I Used to Know could be any one of a great many songwriters. The lyrics are pure and honest, production is sparse at first... and grows as the song progresses with a powerhouse vocal performance on the choruses. Equally powerful vocals on the next track, Eyes Wide Open, which reminds me possibly of Bryan Ferry/Roxy Music. The next, Smoke & Mirrors, is admittedly my probably least favorite on the disc, but is still worth a listen. The next two tracks take a very positive and upbeat turn. I Feel Better sounds like Motown at it's best/happiest with it's synthesized horns and vocals in the vein of Smokey Robinson. In Your Light is equally ebullient with horns and a lively vocal and peppy keyboards. After that, State of the Art is a hilarious track with astounding production that reminds me of Ween's very best work. The next (Don't Worry... We'll Be Watching) is a spare electronica track with a gorgeous creeping bassline and foggy electric sounds behind. The last 3 tracks all have a beautiful melancholy to them but all have their own flow. The closer Bronte is a beautifully emotional piece indicative of what Gotye seems best at - taking a somewhat simple or typical subject and creating a gorgeous piece of music out of. He takes the simplest, most basic building blocks of a song and places them at the core of the music, weaving simply effective layers around those. This disc is an example of mastering that craft. It's the best record I think I've heard in the last year or more. Truly a great piece of work. Listen to it with headphones and pay attention. You will be greatly rewarded.

0060558121|3.0|This is a very well written book as I am sure many would agree. And the premise of this book is absolutely brilliant, and very relevant to our current times. However, the execution was very difficult for me personally, to grasp.<br /><br />The main concept of the novel is that gods and mythological creatures, in general, exist because people believe in them. Immigrants to the US brought with them all sorts of creatures (or Gods, if you will). You had the dwarves, elves, leprechauns, the jin and many other spirits and gods. However, it seems that in present-day America, the power of these mythological beings has diminished greatly as people's beliefs wane. These Gods, referred to as the 'Old Gods', are starting to disappear, or more like they are being forgotten, as new gods take their place.<br /><br />Those new gods are a reflection of America's obsessions with media, celebrity, technology, internet, among others - so you have the God of Media, the God of Radio, the God of Television, the God of Internet etc.<br /><br />The 'Old Gods' led by Odin (the All-Father) want to participate in an epic battle against the New Gods hoping to restore their standing.<br /><br />The story revolves around a central character, Shadow, who is just released from prison to find that his wife had died in a tragic car accident with his best friend Robbie, and that she had been cheating on him with said friend. He is then approached by a mysterious man who goes by the name of Mr. Wednesday. Wednesday offers Shadow a job of becoming his protector - or bodyguard - but is not allowed to ask questions throughout their journey. And so begins Shadow's trek across the United States as he meets Wednesday's bizarre acquaintances and all the different creatures and Gods.<br /><br />As mentioned, the basis of the story is exceptional, but unfortunately, I just felt like the story went on for far too long. The events taking place were very slow, it took me a while to understand what was happening, or why it was happening. There was so much going on all at the same time. It's impressive the way Neil Gaiman managed to put it all together, but it did not attract me as a reader. It honestly took me so long to finish this book, and once I put it down, all I felt was relief that it was finally over.<br /><br />My favourite part of the entire story was the Introductory Note by Neil Gaiman, as I had bought the 10th Anniversary Edition. At one point he writes that the reception this book got were of two extremes: you either loved it, or hated it.<br /><br />Well, I suppose I'm here to tip the balance, as I neither loved it nor hated it. I liked it well enough.n all at the same time. It's impressive the way Neil Gaiman managed to put it all together, but it did not attract me as a reader. It honestly took me so long to finish this book, and once I put it down, all I felt was relief that it was finally over. B004Q7CIFI|5.0|I have read many of Stephen King's books. I'm a big fan of his writing style, and it's gotten to the point where I can generally see where the writer is going to go throughout the course of his novels. Such was the case with this book. Fortunately, that didn't matter one bit.  King develops his characters so naturally and so masterfully that it almost makes the setting and the subject of this novel secondary to the interpersonal relationships, which is the whole point, I suppose. Never in a Stephen King book have I read such a moving romance element; his Jake Epping falls into a relationship so effortlessly and convincingly that it honestly took me by surprise. It is far from uncommon for him to provide a romantic interest for his characters, but it's never seemed like he has taken it so seriously as in \\"11/22/63\\". I found myself extremely charmed and emotionally invested in the main character, as well as the small town community of Jodie (the small town outside of Dallas where he bides his time), which makes up most of the supporting cast.  King clearly performed a lot of research in his process for writing the novel. While I wasn't there, I have a very clear picture of his 1950s-60s, and the minutiae involving the movements and habits of Lee Oswald is interesting. As in any work of fiction that attempts to tell history, there are some inaccuracies, which the author disclaims in his afterword. There are times when the historical aspects of the novel become a bit dry; generally the King does a fine job of intertwining the fictional elements of his story well enough to keep both subjects in the front of the reader's mind.  In the end what the novel comes down to is (like any story worth telling) the characters. I'd be lying if I were to say that part of me (most of me) didn't want Jake to just settle down and forgo his mission. The novel is a very entertaining foray into historical fiction and an interesting change of scenery for Mr. King. Of course, the novel stillfeatures a writer/teacher from Maine, but he's a very relatable teacher that made it easy to relate.  This book is very accessible to a broad range of audiences. If you enjoy good stories, you'll enjoy this one. Give it a read.

B006UG90RM|3.0|Well, I can't believe my eyes. Do I see over 400 reviews of \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" here? It's nice to see there are still people who listen to Van Halen. My guess is we're all mostly long time hardcore fans because I doubt very many kids born 1988 or later even know who Van Halen are unless their parents played something for them. \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" shot straight to number 2 on the Billboard Hot 200 albums chart. Not bad for a 14 year absence.<br /><br />And what about David Lee Roth returning to the fold? Something us fans had been hoping for since 1985. I listened to \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" multiple times, plus I went back and listened to all of Van Halen's albums in sequential order to refresh my mind, plus I read the negative and positive reviews here. While I understand some reviewers were unimpressed with David Lee Roth's vocals, I felt his vocals were the same as they had always been. I think those reviewers were being melodramatic. This is David Lee Roth, not Sammy Hagar, not Gary Cherone. The party atmosphere of the old Van Halen has returned with Roth here.<br /><br />That being said, I do have to agree with the critical reviewers that \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" is not Van Halen's best work. I also agree that nearly everything Eddie and Alex do here is something we've already heard before. I agree that both of them didn't really stretch and experiment too much this time around. \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" is just Van Halen doing Van Halen. It's a straightforward rock and roll album. That's it. Nothing more.<br /><br />I don't know if Michael Anthony is entirely missed here. Wolfgang does a suitable job on bass and background/harmony vocals.<br /><br />The lyrics are pure Roth/Van Halen. I mean a song about tattoos? A prostitute? Drugs and partying? Avoiding work? Mullets? It's all here in pure Roth/Van Halen style.<br /><br />Now, fans are going to be opinionated about what the best tracks are here, but the truth is, in today's narrow radio markets, I don't hear any real hits. Yes, you heard me. That's right. No real hits here. I didn't think there were any real hits on \\"Van Halen III\\" either, and I was right--no top 40 hits. I don't know if it's intentional, or if the band just can't make hits anymore. There are good songs, however, like \\"Tattoo\\", \\"You And Your Blues\\", \\"China Town\\", \\"Blood And Fire\\", \\"As Is\\", \\"Stay Frosty\\" and \\"Big River\\", but they're all not going to make smash hits on the radio (or MTV/VH1 either). The only place \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" will be a hit is with Van Halen fans (and judging by all the mixed reviews here, that's bound to be a split too).<br /><br />So, nothing new here, but Van Halen sounds promising with their first album in 14 years. Let's hope they make some more. I could see them working out the rust found here. Still, there is no band quite like Van Halen, not even today. They are one of a kind, and it's good to have them back with Roth, but I feel they are going to have to try harder than \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" if they are going to truly make a comeback.<br /><br />Here's how \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" compares to the band's previous works:<br /><br />1978 Van Halen: Five Stars<br />1979 Van Halen II: Three and a Half Stars<br />1980 Women And Children First: Four Stars<br />1981 Fair Warning: Four and a Half Stars<br />1982 Diver Down: Four Stars<br />1984 1984: Five Stars<br />1986 5150: Five Stars<br />1988 OU812: Four Stars<br />1991 For Unlawful Carnal Knowledge: Three and a Half Stars<br />1995 Balance: Two and a Half Stars<br />1998 Van Halen III: Two and a Half Stars<br />2012 A Different Kind Of Truth: Three Starsheard me. That's right. No real hits here. I didn't think there were any real hits on \\"Van Halen III\\" either, and I was right--no top 40 hits. I don't know if it's intentional, or if the band just can't make hits anymore. There are good songs, however, like \\"Tattoo\\", \\"You And Your Blues\\", \\"China Town\\", \\"Blood And Fire\\", \\"As Is\\", \\"Stay Frosty\\" and \\"Big River\\", but they're all not going to make smash hits on the radio (or MTV/VH1 either). The only place \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" will be a hit is with Van Halen fans (and judging by all the mixed reviews here, that's bound to be a split too).  So, nothing new here, but Van Halen sounds promising with their first album in 14 years. Let's hope they make some more. I could see them working out the rust found here. Still, there is no band quite like Van Halen, not even today. They are one of a kind, and it's good to have them back with Roth, but I feel they are going to have to try harder than \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" if they are going to truly make a comeback.  Here's how \\"A Different Kind Of Truth\\" compares to the band's previous works:  1978 Van Halen: Five Stars  1979 Van Halen II: Three and a Half Stars  1980 Women And Children First: Four Stars  1981 Fair Warning: Four and a Half Stars  1982 Diver Down: Four Stars  1984 1984: Five Stars  1986 5150: Five Stars  1988 OU812: Four Stars  1991 For Unlawful Carnal Knowledge: Three and a Half Stars  1995 Balance: Two and a Half Stars  1998 Van Halen III: Two and a Half Stars  2012 A Different Kind Of Truth: Three Stars

B00005JKJA|1.0|Though I loved Blue Velvet - at least with this one you could follow its convoluted plot amid all the \\"weird\\" goings on - I'm afraid this one left me cold. At first, I found myself irritated by the leading character's \\"naivete\\" - why didn't she just call the cops? But I know this never happens in movies. In Blue Velvet, the main character gets into deep waters as he takes it upon himself to \\"investigate\\" something he has no business getting involved in to begin with. Typical suspense ploy done to death by Mr Hitch, that requires the viewer to end up identifying with the main character's jeopardy - and one always does, that's the power of movies - and clever directors. Well, by the time I realized that Mullholland Drive was, first, the idealized fantasy the main character has about herself (helping another female in distress to the point of falling in love with her), then a nightmare about guilt, and that she in fact had caused the demise of the \\"one that got away,\\" I thought to myself, oh, here we go again, another cliched swipe at lesbians. Though this one dispenses with the usual icepick, she nevertheless hires a hitman to take care of her treacherous innamorata. And this took two and a half hours to tell. Yes, it's all dazzling to look at, spookily scored, and with the usual Lynchesque gallerie of grotesques, but it's way too long for the tale told. Sometimes Weird for its own sake can be its own worst enemy. I'm afraid that's the case here. Strictly for fanatical Lynch fans and straight men who get off watching Saphic sex in all its splendor, then fantasizing that one of the gals will end up \\"doing the right thing\\" and marrying a guy, and that the one dumped goes bonkers and kills the \\"object of her affection\\", rather than see her \\"be happy,\\" - thus \\"proving,\\" I guess, that Lesbians are sore losers. It's nothing more than Basic Instinct all over again, liberally doused with torrents of Felliana. As for myself, I'll take Vertigo any day.

B000LPR9ZS|5.0|All I can say is \\"WOW!\\" I loved the third installment of the Saw franchise. It's packed with gore and scenes that will make you cringe and look away. Amongst this thick-with-blood film, we have another unique story with yet another climatic twist at the end. \\"Saw III\\" picks up where \\"Saw II\\" left off and if you haven't seen the first two Saw movies, I strongly recommend that you watch them first. You'll see through flashbacks to the previous two Saw movies how \\"Saw III\\" fits together with the other two like a puzzle piece, so all three are linked together perfectly.  Amanda (Shawnee Smith) is back once again and she's vicious! She is a very strong and pivotal character in the film, and Smith does an outstanding job of portraying the violent, emotionally unstable Amanda. As Jigsaw's/John Kramer's accomplice, she is helping him with his latest game, but it's Amanda who is truly put to the test as you will see as the film progresses. John is bedridden, hooked up to a heart monitor, dying from cancer and using an oxygen mask to help him breathe, however he uses his bleak situation as a tool for his game. Amanda kidnaps a woman named Lynn (Bahar Soomekh), a depressed, pill-popping surgeon with marital problems, and takes her to the building where John lays waiting. Lynn's test? Keep John alive until another person in the building completes his series of tests. But it won't be that easy. John will need brain surgery and fast (the brain surgery segment is probably my favorite part in the film). Lynn must do the gruesome surgery and keep John from flat lining, or else the shotgun collar that Amanda placed around her head will go off, and she too will flat line.  The other person going through his own tests is a man named Jeff (Angus Macfadyen), a grieving father whose son was hit and killed by a drunk driver. Ever since the tragedy, Jeff has become bitter and emotionally lost, clinging to his deceased son's toys, neglecting his daughter and obsessing about revenge on thoseresponsible for what happened. But Jigsaw has made the perfect game for Jeff, where he will have the ultimate choice to forgive and let go, or continue to let his hatred and hunger for revenge consume him. Jeff will come face to face with all those involved in his son's untimely death; the only witness to the crime who ran from the scene, the judge who gave the driver a light sentence, and finally the man responsible for the death of his son. All are in their own Jigsaw traps and it's up to Jeff whether they live or die. We're treated to some new inventive traps; the Freezing room trap, the pig juice vat trap and the Rack trap that twists limbs.  So the web of John, Amanda, Jeff and Lynn make \\"Saw III\\" what it is. However there are some other main factors of the movie that are brought to our attention at the start of the film. Take the situation of Troy (J. Larose), a man who seemingly enjoys being in prison more than having freedom. Troy is in a chain trap, where the chains are literally hooked into various areas of his body. He must release himself before a bomb goes off. But we'll find out that there is something different about this particular Jigsaw trap; something that doesn't ring true to Jigsaw's philosophy of earning the privilege to stay alive. Such is also the case with detective Alison Kerry (Dina Meyer), the ever devoted crime investigator from the first two Saw movies who blames herself for the disappearance of detective Eric Matthews (Donnie Whalberg) (yes, he's back for \\"Saw III\\"). According to Jigsaw, she is as dead as the corpses she investigates and therefore has the opportunity to join death as well. She has been put into a \\"ribcage angel trap\\", where there is a device hooked into her ribcage. She must unlock the device with a key that is inside a beaker of acid within a minute or else......well, you get the picture. But again, this Jigsaw trap is not your average Jigsaw trap. It's seemingly a whole different game.  Fantastic special effects, great acting, intense storyline, new twists, heart-pounding sequences, gore galore and an amazing ending; yes, \\"Saw III\\" more than delivers. Writers Leigh Whannell (who also appears in a key sequence of this film) and James Wan do it again, and Darren Lynn Bousman is back as director. They do an excellent job of bringing \\"Saw III\\" together with the first two. As much as I like the first Saw, this one probably beats it out by a hair. \\"Saw III\\" is horror at its best. You don't want to miss it.
